A belated notes file.
-----
VERSION SKEW!! ARGHHH!!!!

I seem to have a number of different versions of MIT Scheme
on my machine, and I seem to have problems with most of them.

Microcode
    c:\Program Files\MIT\bin\bchschem.exe             973074  Feb 13 2007   7.8.0 / 14.11
    c:\Program Files\MIT\bin\old-bchschem.exe        1173258  Jun 16 2002   7.7.0 / -----
    c:\Program Files\MIT\bin\scheme.exe               936466  Jun 23 2007   7.8.0 / 14.11
    c:\Program Files\MIT\Scheme\bin\bchscheme.exe    1137922  Jan 30 2004   7.7.1 / -----
    c:\Program Files\MIT\Scheme\bin\newscheme.exe    1120034  Apr 30 2004   7.7.1 / -----
    c:\Program Files\MIT\Scheme\bin\old-bchschem.exe 1173258  Jun 16 2002   7.7.0 / -----
    c:\Program Files\MIT\Scheme\bin\old-scheme.exe   1155874  Jun 16 2002   7.7.0 / -----
    c:\Program Files\MIT\Scheme\bin\scheme.exe	     1120034  Jan 30 2004   7.7.1 / -----

Heap Images
    c:\Program Files\MIT\lib\all.com                10717436  Feb 05 2007
    c:\Program Files\MIT\lib\runtime.com             3918056  Feb 03 2006
    c:\Program Files\MIT\Scheme\lib\all.com          9557012  Jun 17 2002
    c:\Program Files\MIT\Scheme\lib\runtime.com      3369824  Jun 17 2002


I set up link to run bchscheme from the start menu.  It is set up to run

    c:\Program Files\MIT\bin\bchschem.exe --library "C:\Program Files\MIT\lib" --compiler --heap 11100 --edwin --edit

and this reliably works to run
    Release 7.7.90.+
    Microcode 14.18
    Runtime 15.7
    Win32 1.8
    SF 4.41
    Liar 4.118
    Edwin 3.116

This version
    c:\Program Files\MIT\bin\scheme.exe

appears to boot, but immediately gets an access violation upon typing the first close paren.
It doesn't make sense to keep around the ancient versions, so off they go.

The runtime.com band gets an access violation right away.

The problem with this setup is that there isn't much heap and it seems
that the fasdumper has problems.  Every fasdumped file seems to be
exactly 65536 bytes long and the runtime.pkd file is malformatted.

Here's an idea:  get the bin files from the latest Unix/C distribution.
I've got that running on my linux box at work.

--------
Now I have to go back and yank out the slow debugging code.
--------
Ok, this is bizarre.  

The CLR has immutable strings and a way to intern them.  For all
intents and purposes, CLR strings are equivalent to Scheme symbols.
It is natural to use them as the implementation for symbols.

The CLR also has uninterned strings.  A string created at runtime will
be uninterned unless the String.Intern function is invoked.  It seems
natural to use uninterned strings as the implementation for uninterned
symbols.

MIT-Scheme uses uninterned symbols when analyzing the source code.
This is done to give each binding a unique name.  After expanding
macros, the unique names are mapped back to the original names
provided that it does not cause a name conflict.  If the names would
conflict, a new symbol is generated for that binding.

The bug was that the name conflict machinery was sometimes determining
that there was a conflict where there was in fact none.  So when
the renaming code encountered the X in the body of (lambda (x) x), it
determined that it was a different X from the binding of X, and
therefore renamed it.

I had suspected a bug in the hash tables because that was where the
renaming information was stored.

(current-time-string)"Thu Jul 16 08:14:24 2009"

So let's look at ASSQ:

(define (%assoc key alist = caller)
  (lambda (key alist = caller)
    ((lambda (lose)
       ((lambda ()
         ((lambda (loop)
           (set! loop (lambda (alist)
                        (if (pair? alist)  ;; arg0
			  (begin
			    (if (not (pair? (car alist)))
				(lose))
			    (if (= (car (car alist)) key)  ;; deep
				(car alist)
				(loop (cdr alist)))) ;; lexical 1
			  (begin
			    (if (not (null? alist))
				(lose))
			    #f))))
             loop) #!unassigned)) alist))
       (lambda () (error:not-alist alist caller)))))
